class="kt-inside-inner-col"><style>.topic-of-the-day-card .card-body::-webkit-scrollbar{width:8px}.topic-of-the-day-card .card-body::-webkit-scrollbar-track{background:#f1f1f1;border-radius:10px}.topic-of-the-day-card .card-body::-webkit-scrollbar-thumb{background:#a0a0a0;border-radius:10px}.topic-of-the-day-card .card-body::-webkit-scrollbar-thumb:hover{background:#888}.custom-bullet-list{list-style:none;padding-left:0;margin:0}.custom-bullet-list li{padding-left:20px;position:relative;margin-bottom:4px;font-size:14px;line-height:1.6}.custom-bullet-list li::before{content:'•';position:absolute;left:0;top:-9px;font-size:25px;color:#000}.social-links-container{display:flex;justify-content:center;align-items:center;gap:15px;flex-wrap:wrap}@media (max-width:767px){.topic-of-the-day-card{margin-left:15px;margin-right:15px;width:auto}.question-heading{font-size:16px!important}}</style><div
class="topic-of-the-day-card" style="background-color: #fff; border: 1px solid #e0e0e0; border-radius: 8px; box-shadow: 0 4px 10px rgba(0, 0, 0, 0.05); padding: 0; max-width: 100%; box-sizing: border-box; font-family: 'Noto Sans Devanagari', sans-serif; max-height: 507px; display: flex; flex-direction: column;"><div
class="card-header" style="background-color: #8E44AD; padding: 14px 20px; border-top-left-radius: 8px; border-top-right-radius: 8px; display: flex; align-items: center; justify-content: space-between; flex-shrink: 0;"><h3 style="font-size: 18px; margin: 0; font-weight: 700; text-shadow: 1px 1px 2px rgba(0,0,0,0.2); color: white;">
📖 Topic of the Day</h3>
<span
style="font-size: 12px; font-weight: 400; color: white;">
February 24, 2026
</span></div><div
class="card-body" style="padding: 20px; color: black; overflow-y: auto; flex-grow: 1; -webkit-overflow-scrolling: touch; scrollbar-width: thin; scrollbar-color: #a0a0a0 #f1f1f1;"><h4 style="font-size: 18px; font-weight: 600; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 4px; color: #8E44AD;"><u>General Science: Human Blood &#038; Circulation</u></h4><p
style="font-size: 14px; line-height: 1.6; margin-bottom: 10px;">Blood is a <b>fluid connective tissue</b> that circulates in the body, delivering nutrients and oxygen to cells. An average adult has about <b>5 to 6 litres</b> of blood.</p><h4 style="font-size: 17px; margin-top: 30px; margin-bottom: 4px; font-weight: 500; color: #8E44AD;"><u>Composition of Blood</u></h4><ul
class="custom-bullet-list"><li><b>Plasma:</b> The liquid part (55%), containing water, proteins, and salts.</li><li><b>RBCs (Erythrocytes):</b> Contain <b>Hemoglobin</b> for oxygen transport; lifespan of ~120 days.</li><li><b>WBCs (Leukocytes):</b> Act as the body&#8217;s defense system against infections.</li><li><b>Platelets (Thrombocytes):</b> Essential for <b>blood clotting</b> (coagulation).</li></ul><h4 style="font-size: 17px; margin-top: 30px; margin-bottom: 4px; font-weight: 500; color: #8E44AD;"><u>Blood Groups &#038; Types</u></h4><ul
class="custom-bullet-list"><li><b>ABO System:</b> Discovered by <b>Karl Landsteiner</b>. Blood groups are A, B, AB, and O.</li><li><b>Universal Donor:</b> Blood group <b>O negative (O-)</b> can be given to anyone.</li><li><b>Universal Recipient:</b> Blood group <b>AB positive (AB+)</b> can receive from anyone.</li><li><b>Blood pH:</b> Human blood is slightly basic with a pH of approximately <b>7.4</b>.</li></ul><div
style="text-align: center; margin-top: 25px; margin-bottom: 25px;"><h4 class="question-heading" style="color: #8E44AD; font-size: 18px; font-weight: 600; margin-bottom: 10px;">
<u>Question for you</u>: Which vitamin is primarily responsible for helping blood to clot properly after an injury?</h4><p
style="font-size: 18px; font-weight: bold; color: #007bff; margin-bottom: 20px; margin-top: 20px;">
Let us know your answer on our social media! 👇</p><div
class="social-links-container">

createQuiz(containerId,quizData,marksPerQuestion,negativeMarkingRatio){const quizContainer=document.getElementById(containerId);if(!quizContainer){console.error(`Quiz container with ID "${containerId}" not found.`);return}
const quizSection=quizContainer.querySelector('.quiz-section');const resultContainer=quizContainer.querySelector('.result-container');const questionText=quizContainer.querySelector('.question-text');const optionsList=quizContainer.querySelector('.options-list');const pagination=quizContainer.querySelector('.quiz-pagination');const prevBtn=quizContainer.querySelector('.prev-btn');const nextBtn=quizContainer.querySelector('.next-btn');const finishBtn=quizContainer.querySelector('.finish-btn');const restartBtn=resultContainer.querySelector('.restart-btn');let currentQuestionIndex=0;let userAnswers=new Array(quizData.length).fill(null);function loadQuestion(index){optionsList.innerHTML='';const currentQuestion=quizData[index];questionText.innerHTML=`Q${index + 1}: ${currentQuestion.question}`;currentQuestion.options.forEach((option,optionIndex)=>{const li=document.createElement('li');li.innerHTML=`<label><input type="radio" name="${containerId}-q${index}" value="${optionIndex}"><span class="custom-radio"></span><span>${option}</span></label>`;optionsList.appendChild(li);if(userAnswers[index]===optionIndex){li.querySelector('input').checked=!0}});updatePagination();updateButtonVisibility()}
function updatePagination(){pagination.innerHTML='';quizData.forEach((_,i)=>{const pageNum=document.createElement('span');pageNum.className='page-number';if(i===currentQuestionIndex){pageNum.classList.add('active')}
pageNum.textContent=i+1;pagination.appendChild(pageNum)})}
function updateButtonVisibility(){prevBtn.style.visibility=(currentQuestionIndex===0)?'hidden':'visible';nextBtn.style.display=(currentQuestionIndex===quizData.length-1)?'none':'inline-block'}
async function downloadPDF(){const{jsPDF}=window.jspdf;const resultBody=resultContainer.querySelector('.result-body');const reviewContainer=resultContainer.querySelector('.review-container');const quizTitle=quizContainer.querySelector('.quiz-header h3').textContent;const downloadBtn=resultContainer.querySelector('.download-btn');downloadBtn.disabled=!0;resultBody.classList.add('pdf-export-mode');await new Promise(resolve=>setTimeout(resolve,500));const pdf=new jsPDF('p','mm','a4');const pdfWidth=pdf.internal.pageSize.getWidth();const pdfPageHeight=pdf.internal.pageSize.getHeight();const margin=10;const contentWidth=pdfWidth-(margin*2);let yPosition=margin;const questionBlocks=reviewContainer.querySelectorAll('.review-question-block');const totalBlocks=questionBlocks.length;let currentBlock=0;for(const block of questionBlocks){currentBlock++;let percentage=Math.round((currentBlock/totalBlocks)*100);downloadBtn.textContent=`Generating... ${percentage}%`;const canvas=await html2canvas(block,{scale:3,useCORS:!0});const imgWidth=canvas.width;const imgHeight=canvas.height;const aspectRatio=imgHeight/imgWidth;const blockHeightInMM=contentWidth*aspectRatio;if(yPosition>margin&&(yPosition+blockHeightInMM>pdfPageHeight-margin)){pdf.addPage();yPosition=margin}
let finalHeight=blockHeightInMM;if(blockHeightInMM>(pdfPageHeight-margin*2)){finalHeight=(pdfPageHeight-margin*2)}
pdf.addImage(canvas.toDataURL('image/png'),'PNG',margin,yPosition,contentWidth,finalHeight);yPosition+=finalHeight+5}
pdf.save(`${quizTitle}-Results.pdf`);resultBody.classList.remove('pdf-export-mode');downloadBtn.textContent='Download PDF';downloadBtn.disabled=!1}
function showResults(){let score=0;const negativeMark=marksPerQuestion*negativeMarkingRatio;userAnswers.forEach((answer,index)=>{if(answer!==null){if(answer===quizData[index].answer){score+=marksPerQuestion}else{score-=negativeMark}}});const totalMarks=quizData.length*marksPerQuestion;const resultHeading=resultContainer.querySelector('.result-heading');const scoreText=resultContainer.querySelector('.score-text');const feedbackMessage=resultContainer.querySelector('.feedback-message');const reviewContainer=resultContainer.querySelector('.review-container');const percentage=(score/totalMarks)*100;let message='';if(percentage>=90){message="Excellent! You have a brilliant command of the subject. Keep up the fantastic work! 🏆"}else if(percentage>=80){message="Great job! Your performance was very strong. A little more revision and you'll be at the top! 👍"}else if(percentage>=70){message="Good effort! You have a solid understanding of the concepts. Keep practicing to improve further. 😊"}else if(percentage>=60){message="Well done! You have a good grasp of the basics. Focus on revising the weaker areas. 🙂"}else if(percentage>=50){message="You're on the right track! This is a decent score. Analyze your mistakes and try again. 💪"}else if(percentage>=40){message="Keep practicing. You've built a foundation. Consistent effort will bring better results. 📚"}else{message="Keep pushing forward! 🚀 Every quiz is a learning opportunity. Analyze your mistakes, revise the concepts, and you will surely excel in your next attempt."}
resultHeading.textContent='Quiz Completed!';scoreText.textContent=`Your Score: ${score.toFixed(2)} out of ${totalMarks.toFixed(2)}`;feedbackMessage.innerHTML=message;reviewContainer.innerHTML='';quizData.forEach((question,index)=>{let optionsHTML='';question.options.forEach((option,optionIndex)=>{let liClass='';if(optionIndex===question.answer){liClass='correct-answer'}else if(optionIndex===userAnswers[index]){liClass='wrong-answer'}
optionsHTML+=`<li class="${liClass}">${option}</li>`});let formattedExplanation=question.explanation.replace(/ (Statement|Conclusion|Therefore)/g,'<br><br>$1');reviewContainer.innerHTML+=`
                    <div class="review-question-block">
                        <h5>Q${index + 1}: ${question.question}</h5>
                        <ul class="review-options-list">${optionsHTML}</ul>
                        <div class="explanation-box"><strong><u>Detailed Answer</u>:</strong><br>${formattedExplanation}</div>
                    </div>`});if(window.MathJax){MathJax.typesetPromise([reviewContainer]).catch((err)=>console.log('MathJax error:',err))}
const resultFooter=resultContainer.querySelector('.result-footer');resultFooter.innerHTML='<button class="restart-btn">Attempt Again</button><button class="download-btn">Download PDF</button>';resultFooter.querySelector('.restart-btn').addEventListener('click',restartQuiz);resultFooter.querySelector('.download-btn').addEventListener('click',downloadPDF);quizSection.classList.add('hidden');resultContainer.classList.remove('hidden')}
function restartQuiz(){currentQuestionIndex=0;userAnswers.fill(null);resultContainer.classList.add('hidden');quizSection.classList.remove('hidden');loadQuestion(currentQuestionIndex)}
optionsList.addEventListener('change',(event)=>{if(event.target.type==='radio'){userAnswers[currentQuestionIndex]=parseInt(event.target.value)}});nextBtn.addEventListener('click',()=>{if(currentQuestionIndex<quizData.length-1){currentQuestionIndex++;loadQuestion(currentQuestionIndex)}});prevBtn.addEventListener('click',()=>{if(currentQuestionIndex>0){currentQuestionIndex--;loadQuestion(currentQuestionIndex)}});finishBtn.addEventListener('click',showResults);restartBtn.addEventListener('click',restartQuiz);loadQuestion(currentQuestionIndex)}

In 34x5y, the last two digits are 5y. The multiples of 4 that start with 5 are:<ul><li>52 (since 4 &times; 13 = 52)</li><li>56 (since 4 &times; 14 = 56)</li></ul>Thus, the possible values for y are 2 and 6.<br><br><b>Step 2: Divisibility by 9</b><br>A number is divisible by 9 if the sum of its digits is divisible by 9. Sum of digits of 34x5y = 3 + 4 + x + 5 + y = 12 + x + y.<br>Now, let's test our two cases for y:<br><br><b>Case 1: If y = 2</b><br>Sum of digits = 12 + x + 2 = 14 + x. For (14 + x) to be divisible by 9, x must be 4 (because 14 + 4 = 18, which is a multiple of 9).<br>Pair found: (4, 2).<br><br><b>Case 2: If y = 6</b><br>Sum of digits = 12 + x + 6 = 18 + x. For (18 + x) to be divisible by 9, x can be:<ul><li>0 (because 18 + 0 = 18, which is a multiple of 9).</li><li>9 (because 18 + 9 = 27, which is a multiple of 9).</li></ul>Pairs found: (0, 6) and (9, 6).<br><br><b>Conclusion:</b> The possible pairs of (x, y) are (4, 2), (0, 6), and (9, 6). In total, there are 3 such pairs.<br><br><b>Correct Answer: (B) 3</b>"},{"question":"A committee of 5 members is to be formed from 5 Men and 4 Women. In how many ways can the committee be formed such that it contains at least 2 men and at least 2 women?","options":["(A) 60","(B) 80","(C) 100","(D) 120"],"answer":2,"explanation":"To find the number of ways to form the committee, we first identify all the possible combinations of men and women that satisfy the condition \"at least 2 men and at least 2 women\" for a committee of 5 members.<br><br>Given: Total Men = 5, Total Women = 4, Committee size = 5.<br><br><b>Step 1: Identify the possible cases</b><br>Since the committee must have at least 2 of each gender, the only possible combinations are:<ul><li>Case 1: 2 Men and 3 Women</li><li>Case 2: 3 Men and 2 Women</li></ul>(Note: 4 Men and 1 Woman is not allowed because there must be at least 2 women. Similarly, 1 Man and 4 Women is not allowed because there must be at least 2 men.)<br><br><b>Step 2: Calculate the combinations for Case 1</b><br>Case 1: 2 Men (from 5) and 3 Women (from 4)<ul><li>Ways to choose 2 men: <math><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>5</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>5</mn><mo>&#215;</mo><mn>4</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo>&#215;</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></math></li><li>Ways to choose 3 women: <math><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>4</mn><mn>3</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>4</mn><mn>1</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mn>4</mn></math></li></ul>Total for Case 1: 10 &times; 4 = 40<br><br><b>Step 3: Calculate the combinations for Case 2</b><br>Case 2: 3 Men (from 5) and 2 Women (from 4)<ul><li>Ways to choose 3 men: <math><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>5</mn><mn>3</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>5</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mn>10</mn></math></li><li>Ways to choose 2 women: <math><mfenced><mfrac linethickness=\"0\"><mn>4</mn><mn>2</mn></mfrac></mfenced><mo>=</mo><mfrac><mrow><mn>4</mn><mo>&#215;</mo><mn>3</mn></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><mo>&#215;</mo><mn>1</mn></mrow></mfrac><mo>=</mo><mn>6</mn></math></li></ul>Total for Case 2: 10 &times; 6 = 60<br><br><b>Step 4: Calculate the total number of ways</b><br>Total ways = (Ways from Case 1) + (Ways from Case 2) = 40 + 60 = 100<br><br><b>Correct Answer: (C) 100</b>"},{"question":"<b>Passage:</b><br>The \"Precautionary Principle\" in environmental law suggests that if an action or policy has a suspected risk of causing harm to the public or the environment, in the absence of scientific consensus, the burden of proof falls on those taking the action. Critics argue that this stifles innovation, as absolute certainty of safety is a scientific impossibility. However, proponents argue that the principle is not a \"stop sign\" but a \"caution light\" that shifts the focus from reactive compensation to proactive prevention. The real challenge lies in the disproportionate impact of \"false positives\"—where a safe technology is banned—versus the irreversible damage of \"false negatives\"—where a harmful technology is permitted.<br><br><b>Question:</b> Which of the following is the most valid inference from the passage?","options":["(A) The Precautionary Principle is an anti-science doctrine that prioritizes emotion over evidence.","(B) Scientific consensus is the only reliable basis for making environmental policies.","(C) The principle fundamentally alters the traditional legal assumption of \"innocent until proven guilty\" for new technologies.","(D) False positives in technological regulation are more dangerous than false negatives."],"answer":2,"explanation":"To find the most valid inference, we look for a conclusion that is logically necessitated by the information provided:<br><br><b>The Shift in Burden of Proof:</b> The passage explicitly states that under the Precautionary Principle, the \"burden of proof falls on those taking the action\" in the absence of scientific consensus.<br><br><b>Traditional Logic vs. This Principle:</b> In the traditional legal framework of \"innocent until proven guilty,\" the burden of proof lies with the accuser to prove harm. However, this principle requires the \"actor\" to prove safety before acting. This is a direct reversal of the traditional assumption of \"innocence\" (safety) for new technologies.<br><br><b>Logical Result:</b> Therefore, the most critical structural change described is the alteration of how we assign \"guilt\" or \"harm\" to a new intervention.<br><br><b>Why the other options are incorrect:</b><ul><li>(A) is too extreme and biased. The passage presents both sides and describes the principle as a \"caution light,\" not as \"anti-science.\"</li><li>(B) contradicts the text. The passage explains that the principle is used specifically \"in the absence of scientific consensus.\"</li><li>(D) misinterprets the text. While the passage mentions the tension, it describes false negatives as having \"irreversible damage,\" which usually implies they are more dangerous. In any case, the text doesn't definitively state which is \"more dangerous.\"</li></ul><b>Correct Answer: (C)</b>"},{"question":"<b>Question:</b> Is the positive integer Z a prime number?<br><br><b>Statement I:</b> Z is a factor of (11! + 1).<br><b>Statement II:</b> Z is greater than 11 and less than 20.","options":["(A) Statement I alone is sufficient.","(B) Statement II alone is sufficient.","(C) Both Statement I and Statement II together are sufficient.","(D) Both Statement I and Statement II together are not sufficient."],"answer":2,"explanation":"To determine whether the positive integer Z is a prime number, let's analyze the statements using number theory principles.<br><br><b>Step 1: Analyze Statement I → Z is a factor of (11! + 1).</b><br>(11! + 1) is (1 &times; 2 &times; 3 &times; ... &times; 11) + 1.<br>A key property of factorials is that (n! + 1) is not divisible by any integer from 2 to n.<br>Therefore, any factor of (11! + 1) must be greater than 11.<br>However, being a factor of (11! + 1) does not guarantee that Z is prime.<br>Statement I alone is <b>NOT sufficient</b>.<br><br><b>Step 2: Analyze Statement II → Z is greater than 11 and less than 20.</b><br>The possible values are {12, 13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 18, 19}.<br>In this set, some are prime (13, 17, 19) and some are composite (12, 14, 15, 16, 18).<br>Statement II alone is <b>NOT sufficient</b>.<br><br><b>Step 3: Combine Statement I and Statement II</b><br>From Statement I, we know Z cannot be divisible by any prime number &le; 11 (2, 3, 5, 7, 11).<br>From Statement II, we know Z is in the range (11, 20). Let's check the composite numbers in this range:<ul><li>12: Divisible by 2 and 3.</li><li>14: Divisible by 2 and 7.</li><li>15: Divisible by 3 and 5.</li><li>16: Divisible by 2.</li><li>18: Divisible by 2 and 3.</li></ul>Every composite number between 11 and 20 is composed of prime factors that are all &le; 11. As established, 11! + 1 cannot be divided by any prime &le; 11.<br>Therefore, no composite number in the range (11, 20) can be a factor of (11! + 1).<br>If Z is a factor of (11! + 1) and falls within that range, Z <b>must</b> be one of the prime numbers (13, 17, or 19).<br><br><b>Conclusion:</b> By combining the statements, we can definitively say that Z must be prime.<br><br><b>Correct Answer: (C) Both Statement I and Statement II together are sufficient.</b>"}];createQuiz('gs-quiz',gsQuizData,2,1/3);createQuiz('csat-quiz',csatQuizData,2.5,1/3)</script> <style>.kadence-force-border{border:2px solid #AF1794!important}@media (max-width:768px){.kadence-force-border{margin-left:15px!important;margin-right:15px!important}}</style><style>#left-sidebar,#right-sidebar{display:none!important}#primary{width:100%!important;margin:0!important}</style><style>.quiz-cta-button .wp-block-button__link{transition:all 0.3s ease;will-change:transform}.quiz-cta-button .wp-block-button__link:hover{color:#FFFFE0!important;background:#555555!important;transform:translateY(-3px);filter:brightness(90%);box-shadow:0 5px 15px rgb(0 0 0 / .2)}.quiz-cta-button .wp-block-button__link::before{content:'';display:inline-block;background-image:url('data:image/svg+xml,<svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="white"><path d="M5 5v14h3v-2h4l8-5-8-5H8V5H5z"/></svg>');background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:contain;width:1.5em;height:1.5em;margin-right:8px;vertical-align:middle;transform:translateY(-2px)}@media (max-width:768px){.quiz-cta-button .wp-block-button__link{font-size:16px!important;width:100%!important}}</style></div></div></article></main></div></div></div><div
